<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Tuberculosis</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:307px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Depiction_of_a_tuberculosis_patient.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1667" data-file-width="2605" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Depiction_of_a_tuberculosis_patient.png/305px-Depiction_of_a_tuberculosis_patient.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Depiction_of_a_tuberculosis_patient.png/458px-Depiction_of_a_tuberculosis_patient.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Depiction_of_a_tuberculosis_patient.png/610px-Depiction_of_a_tuberculosis_patient.png 2x" width="305"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Depiction_of_a_tuberculosis_patient.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Depiction of a man with tuberculosis</div></div></div>
<p><b>Tuberculosis</b> (<b>TB</b>) is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" title="Infectious disease">infectious disease</a> usually caused by <i><a href="/wiki/Mycobacterium_tuberculosis" title="Mycobacterium tuberculosis">Mycobacterium tuberculosis</a></i> (MTB) <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2015Fact_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015Fact-1">[1]</a></sup> Tuberculosis generally affects the <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">lungs</a>, but it can also affect other parts of the body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2015Fact_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015Fact-1">[1]</a></sup> Most infections show no symptoms, in which case it is known as <a href="/wiki/Latent_tuberculosis" title="Latent tuberculosis">latent tuberculosis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2015Fact_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015Fact-1">[1]</a></sup> Around 10% of latent infections progress to active disease which, if left untreated, kill about half of those affected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2015Fact_1-8"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015Fact-1">[1]</a></sup> Typical symptoms of active TB are chronic <a href="/wiki/Cough" title="Cough">cough</a> with <a href="/wiki/Hemoptysis" title="Hemoptysis">blood-containing</a> <a href="/wiki/Sputum" title="Sputum">mucus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fever" title="Fever">fever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Night_sweats" title="Night sweats">night sweats</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Weight_loss" title="Weight loss">weight loss</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2015Fact_1-9"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015Fact-1">[1]</a></sup> It was historically referred to as <b>consumption</b> due to the weight loss associated with the disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cha1998_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cha1998-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">Infection</a> of other organs can cause a wide range of symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ID10_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-ID10-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tuberculosis is <a href="/wiki/Human-to-human_transmission" title="Human-to-human transmission">spread from one person to the next</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Airborne_disease" title="Airborne disease">through the air</a> when people who have active TB in their lungs cough, spit, speak, or <a href="/wiki/Sneeze" title="Sneeze">sneeze</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2015Fact_1-10"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015Fact-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2012B_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDC2012B-10">[10]</a></sup> People with Latent TB do not spread the disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2015Fact_1-11"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015Fact-1">[1]</a></sup> Active infection occurs more often in people with <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> and in those who <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_smoking" title="Tobacco smoking">smoke</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2015Fact_1-12"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015Fact-1">[1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Diagnosis" title="Diagnosis">Diagnosis</a> of active TB is based on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chest_X-ray" title="Chest X-ray">chest X-rays</a>, as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microscopic" title="Microscopic">microscopic</a> examination and <a href="/wiki/Microbiological_culture" title="Microbiological culture">culture</a> of body fluids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-AP-11">[11]</a></sup> Diagnosis of Latent TB relies on the <a href="/wiki/Mantoux_test" title="Mantoux test">tuberculin skin test</a> (TST) or blood tests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-AP-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>Prevention of TB involves screening those at high risk, early detection and treatment of cases, and <a href="/wiki/Vaccination" title="Vaccination">vaccination</a> with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bacillus_Calmette-Gu%C3%A9rin" title="Bacillus Calmette-Guérin">bacillus Calmette-Guérin</a> (BCG) vaccine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haw2014_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Haw2014-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TBCon2008_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-TBCon2008-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harr2013_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Harr2013-5">[5]</a></sup> Those at high risk include household, workplace, and social contacts of people with active TB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TBCon2008_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-TBCon2008-4">[4]</a></sup> Treatment requires the use of multiple <a href="/wiki/Antibiotic" title="Antibiotic">antibiotics</a> over a long period of time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2015Fact_1-13"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015Fact-1">[1]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antibiotic_resistance" title="Antibiotic resistance">Antibiotic resistance</a> is a growing problem with increasing rates of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi-drug-resistant_tuberculosis" title="Multi-drug-resistant tuberculosis">multiple drug-resistant tuberculosis</a> (MDR-TB).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2015Fact_1-14"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015Fact-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, one quarter of the world's population was thought to have a latent infection of TB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2018Fact_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2018Fact-6">[6]</a></sup> New infections occur in about 1% of the population each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2002_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2002-12">[12]</a></sup> In 2020, an estimated 10 million people developed active TB, resulting in 1.5 million deaths, making it the second leading <a href="/wiki/List_of_causes_of_death_by_rate" title="List of causes of death by rate">cause of death from an infectious disease</a> after <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" title="COVID-19">COVID-19</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2020_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2020-13">[13]</a></sup> As of 2018, most TB cases occurred in the regions of South-East Asia (44%), Africa (24%), and the Western Pacific (18%), with more than 50% of cases being diagnosed in seven countries: India (27%), China (9%), Indonesia (8%), the Philippines (6%), Pakistan (6%), Nigeria (4%), and Bangladesh (4%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2017Report_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2017Report-14">[14]</a></sup> By 2021 the number of new cases each year was decreasing by around 2% annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2020_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2020-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2015Fact_1-15"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2015Fact-1">[1]</a></sup> About 80% of people in many Asian and African countries test positive while 5–10% of people in the United States population test positive via the tuberculin test.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robbins_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Robbins-15">[15]</a></sup> Tuberculosis has been present in humans since <a href="/wiki/Ancient_history" title="Ancient history">ancient times</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet11_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet11-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:305px;"><video class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="135" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="En.Wikipedia-VideoWiki-Tuberculosis.webm" height="170" id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/En.Wikipedia-VideoWiki-Tuberculosis.webm/303px-seek%3D60-En.Wikipedia-VideoWiki-Tuberculosis.webm.jpg" preload="none" width="303"><source data-bandwidth="275707" data-framerate="30" data-height="720" data-shorttitle="WebM source" data-title="Original WebM file, 1,280 × 720 (276 kbps)" data-width="1280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/En.Wikipedia-VideoWiki-Tuberculosis.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/><track data-dir="ltr" kind="subtitles" label="English ‪(en)‬" src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3AEn.Wikipedia-VideoWiki-Tuberculosis.webm&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=vtt&amp;origin=%2A" srclang="en" type="text/vtt"/></video> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:En.Wikipedia-VideoWiki-Tuberculosis.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Video summary (<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:VideoWiki/Tuberculosis" title="Wikipedia:VideoWiki/Tuberculosis">script</a>)</div></div></div>
