<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_tuberculosis" title="History of tuberculosis">History of tuberculosis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mummy_at_British_Museum.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1978" data-file-width="2725" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mummy_at_British_Museum.jpg/220px-Mummy_at_British_Museum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mummy_at_British_Museum.jpg/330px-Mummy_at_British_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Mummy_at_British_Museum.jpg/440px-Mummy_at_British_Museum.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mummy_at_British_Museum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egyptian_mummy" title="Egyptian mummy">Egyptian mummy</a> in the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a> – tubercular decay has been found in the spine.</div></div></div>
<p>Tuberculosis has existed since <a href="/wiki/Ancient_history" title="Ancient history">antiquity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet11_16-21"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet11-16">[16]</a></sup> The oldest unambiguously detected <i>M. tuberculosis</i> gives evidence of the disease in the remains of bison in Wyoming dated to around 17,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> However, whether tuberculosis originated in bovines, then transferred to humans, or whether both bovine and human tuberculosis diverged from a common ancestor, remains unclear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> A comparison of the <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">genes</a> of <i>M. tuberculosis</i> complex (MTBC) in humans to MTBC in animals suggests humans did not acquire MTBC from animals during animal domestication, as researchers previously believed. Both strains of the tuberculosis bacteria share a common ancestor, which could have infected humans even before the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">Neolithic Revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Skeletal remains show some prehistoric humans (4000 <a href="/wiki/Common_Era" title="Common Era">BC</a>) had TB, and researchers have found tubercular decay in the spines of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egyptian</a> <a href="/wiki/Mummy" title="Mummy">mummies</a> dating from 3000 to 2400 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> Genetic studies suggest the presence of TB in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">the Americas</a> from about AD 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup>
</p><p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, folklore often associated tuberculosis with <a href="/wiki/Vampire" title="Vampire">vampires</a>. When one member of a family died from the disease, the other infected members would lose their health slowly. People believed this was caused by the original person with TB draining the life from the other family members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sledzik_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-sledzik-164">[164]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dr_Richard_Morton" title="Dr Richard Morton">Richard Morton</a> established the pulmonary form associated with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tubercle_(anatomy)" title="Tubercle (anatomy)">tubercles</a> as a pathology in 1689,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WhoNamedIt-Calmette_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-WhoNamedIt-Calmette-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MedHist1970-Trail_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-MedHist1970-Trail-166">[166]</a></sup> due to the variety of its symptoms, TB was not identified as a single disease until the 1820s.  <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Marten" title="Benjamin Marten">Benjamin Marten</a> conjectured in 1720 that consumptions were caused by microbes which were spread by people living in close proximity to each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> In 1819 <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Laennec" title="René Laennec">René Laennec</a> claimed that tubercles were the cause of pulmonary tuberculosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Johann_Lukas_Sch%C3%B6nlein" title="Johann Lukas Schönlein">J. L. Schönlein</a> first published the name "tuberculosis" (German:  <i>Tuberkulose</i>) in 1832.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Between 1838 and 1845, John Croghan, the owner of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mammoth_Cave" title="Mammoth Cave">Mammoth Cave</a> in Kentucky from 1839 onwards, brought a number of people with tuberculosis into the cave in the hope of curing the disease with the constant temperature and purity of the cave air; each died within a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> Hermann Brehmer opened the first TB <a href="/wiki/Sanatorium" title="Sanatorium">sanatorium</a> in 1859 in Görbersdorf (now <a href="/wiki/Soko%C5%82owsko" title="Sokołowsko">Sokołowsko</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sanatoria_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-sanatoria-172">[172]</a></sup> In 1865 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean_Antoine_Villemin" title="Jean Antoine Villemin">Jean Antoine Villemin</a> demonstrated that tuberculosis could be transmitted, via inoculation, from humans to animals and among animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> (Villemin's findings were confirmed in 1867 and 1868 by <a href="/wiki/John_Burdon-Sanderson" title="John Burdon-Sanderson">John Burdon-Sanderson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup>)
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RobertKoch.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1452" data-file-width="1008" decoding="async" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/RobertKoch.jpg/170px-RobertKoch.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/RobertKoch.jpg/255px-RobertKoch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/RobertKoch.jpg/340px-RobertKoch.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RobertKoch.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Robert Koch discovered the tuberculosis bacillus.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Robert_Koch" title="Robert Koch">Robert Koch</a> identified and described the bacillus causing tuberculosis, <i>M. tuberculosis</i>, on 24 March 1882.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-discoverydate_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-discoverydate-176">[176]</a></sup> He received the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine</a> in 1905 for this discovery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> Koch did not believe the cattle and human tuberculosis diseases were similar, which delayed the recognition of infected milk as a source of infection. During the first half of the 1900s the risk of transmission from this source was dramatically reduced after the application of the <a href="/wiki/Pasteurization" title="Pasteurization">pasteurization</a> process. Koch announced a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glycerine" title="Glycerine">glycerine</a> extract of the tubercle bacilli as a "remedy" for tuberculosis in 1890, calling it "tuberculin". Although it was not effective, it was later successfully adapted as a screening test for the presence of pre-symptomatic tuberculosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/World_Tuberculosis_Day" title="World Tuberculosis Day">World Tuberculosis Day</a> is marked on 24 March each year, the anniversary of Koch's original scientific announcement.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Albert_Calmette" title="Albert Calmette">Albert Calmette</a> and <a href="/wiki/Camille_Gu%C3%A9rin" title="Camille Guérin">Camille Guérin</a> achieved the first genuine success in immunization against tuberculosis in 1906, using attenuated bovine-strain tuberculosis. It was called <a href="/wiki/BCG_vaccine" title="BCG vaccine">bacille Calmette–Guérin</a> (BCG). The BCG vaccine was first used on humans in 1921 in France,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bonah_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bonah-179">[179]</a></sup> but achieved widespread acceptance in the US, Great Britain, and Germany only after World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Comstock_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-Comstock-180">[180]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tuberculosis caused widespread public concern in the 19th and early 20th centuries as the disease became common among the urban poor. In 1815 one in four deaths in England was due to "consumption". By 1918, TB still caused one in six deaths in France.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> After TB was determined to be contagious, in the 1880s, it was put on a <a href="/wiki/List_of_notifiable_diseases" title="List of notifiable diseases">notifiable-disease</a> list in Britain; campaigns started to stop people from spitting in public places, and the infected poor were "encouraged" to enter <a href="/wiki/Sanatorium" title="Sanatorium">sanatoria</a> that resembled prisons (the sanatoria for the middle and upper classes offered excellent care and constant medical attention).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sanatoria_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-sanatoria-172">[172]</a></sup> Whatever the benefits of the "fresh air" and labor in the sanatoria, even under the best conditions, 50% of those who entered died within five years (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1916).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sanatoria_172-2"><a href="#cite_note-sanatoria-172">[172]</a></sup> When the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_Research_Council_(UK)" title="Medical Research Council (UK)">Medical Research Council</a> formed in Britain in 1913, it initially focused on tuberculosis research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Europe, rates of tuberculosis began to rise in the early 1600s to a peak level in the 1800s, when it caused nearly 25% of all deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> In the 18th and 19th century, <a href="/wiki/History_of_tuberculosis#Epidemic_tuberculosis" title="History of tuberculosis">tuberculosis had become epidemic in Europe</a>, showing a seasonal pattern.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-:02-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-184">[184]</a></sup> By the 1950s mortality in Europe had decreased about 90%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Per2010_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-Per2010-185">[185]</a></sup> Improvements in sanitation, vaccination, and other public-health measures began significantly reducing rates of tuberculosis even before the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Streptomycin" title="Streptomycin">streptomycin</a> and other antibiotics, although the disease remained a significant threat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Per2010_185-1"><a href="#cite_note-Per2010-185">[185]</a></sup> In 1946 the development of the antibiotic streptomycin made effective treatment and cure of TB a reality. Prior to the introduction of this medication, the only treatment was surgical intervention, including the "<a href="/wiki/Pneumothorax" title="Pneumothorax">pneumothorax</a> technique", which involved collapsing an infected lung to "rest" it and to allow tuberculous lesions to heal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p>Because of the emergence of <a href="/wiki/Multidrug-resistant_tuberculosis" title="Multidrug-resistant tuberculosis">multidrug-resistant tuberculosis (MDR-TB)</a>, surgery has been re-introduced for certain cases of TB infections. It involves the removal of infected chest cavities ("bullae") in the lungs to reduce the number of bacteria and to increase exposure of the remaining bacteria to antibiotics in the bloodstream.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> Hopes of eliminating TB ended with the rise of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antibiotic_resistant" title="Antibiotic resistant">drug-resistant</a> strains in the 1980s. The subsequent resurgence of tuberculosis resulted in the declaration of a global health emergency by the World Health Organization (WHO) in 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Names">Names</span></h3>
<p>Tuberculosis has been known by many names from the technical to the familiar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lawlor_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lawlor-189">[189]</a></sup> <span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><i lang="grc-Latn">Phthisis</i></span> (<span title="Ancient Greek (to 1453)-language text"><span lang="grc">Φθισις</span></span>) is a Greek word for consumption, an old term for pulmonary tuberculosis;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cha1998_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cha1998-8">[8]</a></sup> around 460 BCE, <a href="/wiki/Hippocrates" title="Hippocrates">Hippocrates</a> described phthisis as a disease of dry seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> The abbreviation <i>TB</i> is short for <i>tubercle <a href="/wiki/Bacillus_(shape)" title="Bacillus (shape)">bacillus</a></i>. <i>Consumption</i> was the most common nineteenth century English word for the disease. The Latin root <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">con</i></span> meaning 'completely' is linked to <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">sumere</i></span> meaning 'to take up from under'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Life_and_Death_of_Mr_Badman" title="The Life and Death of Mr Badman">The Life and Death of Mr Badman</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/John_Bunyan" title="John Bunyan">John Bunyan</a>, the author calls consumption "the captain of all these men of death."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> "Great white plague" has also been used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lawlor_189-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lawlor-189">[189]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_literature">Art and literature</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Munch_Det_Syke_Barn_1885-86.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="3966" decoding="async" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Munch_Det_Syke_Barn_1885-86.jpg/220px-Munch_Det_Syke_Barn_1885-86.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Munch_Det_Syke_Barn_1885-86.jpg/330px-Munch_Det_Syke_Barn_1885-86.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Munch_Det_Syke_Barn_1885-86.jpg/440px-Munch_Det_Syke_Barn_1885-86.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Munch_Det_Syke_Barn_1885-86.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Painting <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sick_Child_(Munch)" title="The Sick Child (Munch)">The Sick Child</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Edvard_Munch" title="Edvard Munch">Edvard Munch</a>, 1885–86, depicts the illness of his sister Sophie, who died of tuberculosis when Edvard was 14; his mother too died of the disease.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuberculosis_in_human_culture" title="Tuberculosis in human culture">Tuberculosis in human culture</a></div>
<p>Tuberculosis was for centuries associated with <a href="/wiki/Poet" title="Poet">poetic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">artistic</a> qualities among those infected, and was also known as "the romantic disease".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lawlor_189-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lawlor-189">[189]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> Major artistic figures such as the poets <a href="/wiki/John_Keats" title="John Keats">John Keats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Percy_Bysshe_Shelley" title="Percy Bysshe Shelley">Percy Bysshe Shelley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe" title="Edgar Allan Poe">Edgar Allan Poe</a>, the composer <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin" title="Frédéric Chopin">Frédéric Chopin</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IOE_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-IOE-194">[194]</a></sup> the playwright <a href="/wiki/Anton_Chekhov" title="Anton Chekhov">Anton Chekhov</a>, the novelists <a href="/wiki/Franz_Kafka" title="Franz Kafka">Franz Kafka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Mansfield" title="Katherine Mansfield">Katherine Mansfield</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vilaplana2017_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vilaplana2017-195">[195]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Bront%C3%AB" title="Charlotte Brontë">Charlotte Brontë</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Dostoevsky" title="Fyodor Dostoevsky">Fyodor Dostoevsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mann" title="Thomas Mann">Thomas Mann</a>, <a href="/wiki/W._Somerset_Maugham" title="W. Somerset Maugham">W. Somerset Maugham</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rogal1997_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rogal1997-196">[196]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Louis_Stevenson" title="Robert Louis Stevenson">Robert Louis Stevenson</a>, and the artists <a href="/wiki/Alice_Neel" title="Alice Neel">Alice Neel</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JAMA2005_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-JAMA2005-198">[198]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean-Antoine_Watteau" title="Jean-Antoine Watteau">Jean-Antoine Watteau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Siddal" title="Elizabeth Siddal">Elizabeth Siddal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marie_Bashkirtseff" title="Marie Bashkirtseff">Marie Bashkirtseff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edvard_Munch" title="Edvard Munch">Edvard Munch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aubrey_Beardsley" title="Aubrey Beardsley">Aubrey Beardsley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amedeo_Modigliani" title="Amedeo Modigliani">Amedeo Modigliani</a> either had the disease or were surrounded by people who did. A widespread belief was that tuberculosis assisted artistic talent. Physical mechanisms proposed for this effect included the slight fever and toxaemia that it caused, allegedly helping them to see life more clearly and to act decisively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lemlein1981_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lemlein1981-199">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilsey_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wilsey-200">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morens2002_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morens2002-201">[201]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tuberculosis formed an often-reused theme in <a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">literature</a>, as in <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mann" title="Thomas Mann">Thomas Mann</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Mountain" title="The Magic Mountain">The Magic Mountain</a></i>, set in a <a href="/wiki/Sanatorium" title="Sanatorium">sanatorium</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McMasterUni_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-McMasterUni-202">[202]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a>, as in <a href="/wiki/Van_Morrison" title="Van Morrison">Van Morrison</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/T.B._Sheets" title="T.B. Sheets">T.B. Sheets</a>";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a>, as in <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Puccini" title="Giacomo Puccini">Puccini</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/La_boh%C3%A8me" title="La bohème">La bohème</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Verdi" title="Giuseppe Verdi">Verdi</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Traviata" title="La Traviata">La Traviata</a></i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morens2002_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morens2002-201">[201]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a>, as in <a href="/wiki/Claude_Monet" title="Claude Monet">Monet</a>'s painting of his first wife Camille on her deathbed;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAID_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAID-204">[204]</a></sup> and in <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">film</a>, such as the 1945 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bells_of_St._Mary%27s" title="The Bells of St. Mary's">The Bells of St. Mary's</a></i> starring <a href="/wiki/Ingrid_Bergman" title="Ingrid Bergman">Ingrid Bergman</a> as a nun with tuberculosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corliss2008_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-Corliss2008-205">[205]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_health_efforts">Public health efforts</span></h3>
<p>In 2014 the WHO adopted the "End TB" strategy which aims to reduce TB incidence by 80% and TB deaths by 90% by 2030.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who_end_tb_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-who_end_tb-206">[206]</a></sup> The strategy contains a milestone to reduce TB incidence by 20% and TB deaths by 35% by 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2020_TB_report_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-2020_TB_report-207">[207]</a></sup> However, by 2020 only a 9% reduction in incidence per population was achieved globally, with the European region achieving 19% and the African region achieving 16% reductions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2020_TB_report_207-1"><a href="#cite_note-2020_TB_report-207">[207]</a></sup> Similarly, the number of deaths only fell by 14%, missing the 2020 milestone of a 35% reduction, with some regions making better progress (31% reduction in Europe and 19% in Africa).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2020_TB_report_207-2"><a href="#cite_note-2020_TB_report-207">[207]</a></sup> Correspondingly, also treatment, prevention and funding milestones were missed in 2020, for example only 6.3 million people were started on TB prevention short of the target of 30 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2020_TB_report_207-3"><a href="#cite_note-2020_TB_report-207">[207]</a></sup>
</p><p>The World Health Organization (WHO), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bill_and_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" title="Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation">Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation</a>, and the U.S. government are subsidizing a fast-acting diagnostic tuberculosis test for use in low- and middle-income countries as of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PressRelease2012_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-PressRelease2012-208">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Xpert2011_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-Xpert2011-209">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> In addition to being fast-acting, the test can determine if there is resistance to the antibiotic rifampicin which may indicate multi-drug resistant tuberculosis and is accurate in those who are also infected with HIV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PressRelease2012_208-1"><a href="#cite_note-PressRelease2012-208">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> Many resource-poor places as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tuberculosis&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> have access to only sputum microscopy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup>
</p><p>India had the highest total number of TB cases worldwide in 2010, in part due to poor disease management within the private and public health care sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> Programs such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revised_National_Tuberculosis_Control_Program" title="Revised National Tuberculosis Control Program">Revised National Tuberculosis Control Program</a> are working to reduce TB levels among people receiving public health care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bhargava_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bhargava-214">[214]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2014 <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">EIU</a>-healthcare report finds there is a need to address apathy and urges for increased funding. The report cites among others Lucica Ditui "[TB] is like an orphan. It has been neglected even in countries with a high burden and often forgotten by donors and those investing in health interventions."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIU_2014_120-4"><a href="#cite_note-EIU_2014-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>Slow progress has led to frustration, expressed by the executive director of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_Fund_to_Fight_AIDS,_Tuberculosis_and_Malaria" title="Global Fund to Fight AIDS, Tuberculosis and Malaria">Global Fund to Fight AIDS, Tuberculosis and Malaria</a> – Mark Dybul: "we have the tools to end TB as a pandemic and public health threat on the planet, but we are not doing it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIU_2014_120-5"><a href="#cite_note-EIU_2014-120">[120]</a></sup> Several international organizations are pushing for more transparency in treatment, and more countries are implementing mandatory reporting of cases to the government as of 2014, although adherence is often variable. Commercial treatment providers may at times overprescribe second-line drugs as well as supplementary treatment, promoting demands for further regulations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIU_2014_120-6"><a href="#cite_note-EIU_2014-120">[120]</a></sup> The government of Brazil provides universal TB care, which reduces this problem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIU_2014_120-7"><a href="#cite_note-EIU_2014-120">[120]</a></sup> Conversely, falling rates of TB infection may not relate to the number of programs directed at reducing infection rates but may be tied to an increased level of education, income, and health of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIU_2014_120-8"><a href="#cite_note-EIU_2014-120">[120]</a></sup> Costs of the disease, as calculated by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> in 2009 may exceed US$150 billion per year in "high burden" countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIU_2014_120-9"><a href="#cite_note-EIU_2014-120">[120]</a></sup> Lack of progress eradicating the disease may also be due to lack of patient follow-up – as among the 250 million <a href="/wiki/Migration_in_China" title="Migration in China">rural migrants in China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIU_2014_120-10"><a href="#cite_note-EIU_2014-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is insufficient data to show that active contact tracing helps to improve case detection rates for tuberculosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> Interventions such as house-to-house visits, educational leaflets, mass media strategies, educational sessions may increase tuberculosis detection rates in short-term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> There is no study that compares new methods of contact tracing such as social network analysis with existing contact tracing methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stigma">Stigma</span></h3>
<p>Slow progress in preventing the disease may in part be due to <a href="/wiki/Social_stigma" title="Social stigma">stigma</a> associated with TB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIU_2014_120-11"><a href="#cite_note-EIU_2014-120">[120]</a></sup> Stigma may be due to the fear of transmission from affected individuals. This stigma may additionally arise due to links between TB and poverty, and in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS_in_Africa" title="AIDS in Africa">Africa, AIDS</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIU_2014_120-12"><a href="#cite_note-EIU_2014-120">[120]</a></sup> Such stigmatization may be both real and perceived; for example, in Ghana, individuals with TB are banned from attending public gatherings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtwright_2010_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-Courtwright_2010-219">[219]</a></sup>
</p><p>Stigma towards TB may result in delays in seeking treatment,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIU_2014_120-13"><a href="#cite_note-EIU_2014-120">[120]</a></sup> lower treatment compliance, and family members keeping cause of death secret<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtwright_2010_219-1"><a href="#cite_note-Courtwright_2010-219">[219]</a></sup> – allowing the disease to spread further.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIU_2014_120-14"><a href="#cite_note-EIU_2014-120">[120]</a></sup> In contrast, in Russia stigma was associated with increased treatment compliance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtwright_2010_219-2"><a href="#cite_note-Courtwright_2010-219">[219]</a></sup> TB stigma also affects socially marginalized individuals to a greater degree and varies between regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtwright_2010_219-3"><a href="#cite_note-Courtwright_2010-219">[219]</a></sup>
</p><p>One way to decrease stigma may be through the promotion of "TB clubs", where those infected may share experiences and offer support, or through counseling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtwright_2010_219-4"><a href="#cite_note-Courtwright_2010-219">[219]</a></sup> Some studies have shown TB education programs to be effective in decreasing stigma, and may thus be effective in increasing treatment adherence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtwright_2010_219-5"><a href="#cite_note-Courtwright_2010-219">[219]</a></sup> Despite this, studies on the relationship between reduced stigma and mortality are lacking as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tuberculosis&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, and similar efforts to decrease stigma surrounding AIDS have been minimally effective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtwright_2010_219-6"><a href="#cite_note-Courtwright_2010-219">[219]</a></sup> Some have claimed the stigma to be worse than the disease, and healthcare providers may unintentionally reinforce stigma, as those with TB are often perceived as difficult or otherwise undesirable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIU_2014_120-15"><a href="#cite_note-EIU_2014-120">[120]</a></sup> A greater understanding of the social and cultural dimensions of tuberculosis may also help with stigma reduction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/International_Congress_on_Tuberculosis" title="International Congress on Tuberculosis">International Congress on Tuberculosis</a></div>
<p>The BCG vaccine has limitations, and research to develop new TB vaccines is ongoing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VacRes2011_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-VacRes2011-221">[221]</a></sup> A number of potential candidates are currently in <a href="/wiki/Clinical_trial" title="Clinical trial">phase I and II clinical trials</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VacRes2011_221-1"><a href="#cite_note-VacRes2011-221">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> Two main approaches are used to attempt to improve the efficacy of available vaccines. One approach involves adding a subunit vaccine to BCG, while the other strategy is attempting to create new and better live vaccines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VacRes2011_221-2"><a href="#cite_note-VacRes2011-221">[221]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MVA85A" title="MVA85A">MVA85A</a>, an example of a subunit vaccine, is in trials in South Africa as of 2006, is based on a genetically modified <a href="/wiki/Vaccinia" title="Vaccinia">vaccinia</a> virus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ibanga_2006_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ibanga_2006-223">[223]</a></sup> Vaccines are hoped to play a significant role in treatment of both latent and active disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup>
</p><p>To encourage further discovery, researchers and policymakers are promoting new economic models of vaccine development as of 2006, including prizes, tax incentives, and <a href="/wiki/Advance_market_commitments" title="Advance market commitments">advance market commitments</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> A number of groups, including the <a href="/wiki/Stop_TB_Partnership" title="Stop TB Partnership">Stop TB Partnership</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> the South African Tuberculosis Vaccine Initiative, and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Aeras_Global_TB_Vaccine_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Aeras Global TB Vaccine Foundation (page does not exist)">Aeras Global TB Vaccine Foundation</a>, are involved with research.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> Among these, the Aeras Global TB Vaccine Foundation received a gift of more than $280 million (US) from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bill_and_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" title="Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation">Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation</a> to develop and license an improved vaccine against tuberculosis for use in high burden countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup>
</p><p>A number of medications are being studied as of 2012 for multidrug-resistant tuberculosis, including <a href="/wiki/Bedaquiline" title="Bedaquiline">bedaquiline</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delamanid" title="Delamanid">delamanid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zumla2012_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zumla2012-231">[231]</a></sup> Bedaquiline received U.S. <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration" title="Food and Drug Administration">Food and Drug Administration</a> (FDA) approval in late 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> The safety and effectiveness of these new agents are uncertain as of 2012, because they are based on the results of relatively small studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zumla2012_231-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zumla2012-231">[231]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Avorn_2013_1349–1350_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-Avorn_2013_1349–1350-233">[233]</a></sup> However, existing data suggest that patients taking bedaquiline in addition to standard TB therapy are five times more likely to die than those without the new drug,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_Food_and_Drug_Administration_website_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-US_Food_and_Drug_Administration_website-234">[234]</a></sup> which has resulted in medical journal articles raising health policy questions about why the FDA approved the drug and whether financial ties to the company making bedaquiline influenced physicians' support for its use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Avorn_2013_1349–1350_233-1"><a href="#cite_note-Avorn_2013_1349–1350-233">[233]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup>
</p><p>Steroids add-on therapy has not shown any benefits for active pulmonary tuberculosis infection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_animals">Other animals</span></h2>
<p>Mycobacteria infect many different animals, including birds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> fish, rodents,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> and reptiles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> The subspecies <i>Mycobacterium tuberculosis</i>, though, is rarely present in wild animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> An effort to eradicate bovine tuberculosis caused by <i><a href="/wiki/Mycobacterium_bovis" title="Mycobacterium bovis">Mycobacterium bovis</a></i> from the cattle and deer herds of <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> has been relatively successful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> Efforts in Great Britain have been less successful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tuberculosis&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, tuberculosis appears to be widespread among captive <a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">elephants</a> in the US. It is believed that the animals originally acquired the disease from humans, a process called <a href="/wiki/Reverse_zoonosis" title="Reverse zoonosis">reverse zoonosis</a>. Because the disease can spread through the air to infect both humans and other animals, it is a public health concern affecting <a href="/wiki/Circus" title="Circus">circuses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zoo" title="Zoo">zoos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holt_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holt-244">[244]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mikota_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mikota-245">[245]</a></sup>
</p>

</li>

<li id="cite_note-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-53">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFvan_Zyl_SmitPaiYewLeung2010">van Zyl Smit RN, Pai M, Yew WW, Leung CC, Zumla A, Bateman ED,  et al. <li id="cite_note-167"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-167">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFMarten1720">Marten B (1720). <a class="external text" href="https://babel.hathitrust.org/cgi/pt?id=ucm.5320214800&amp;view=1up&amp;seq=7" rel="nofollow"><i>A New Theory of Consumptions—More Especially a Phthisis or Consumption of the Lungs</i></a>. London, England: T. Knaplock.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+New+Theory+of+Consumptions%E2%80%94More+Especially+a+Phthisis+or+Consumption+of+the+Lungs&amp;rft.place=London%2C+England&amp;rft.pub=T.+Knaplock&amp;rft.date=1720&amp;rft.aulast=Marten&amp;rft.aufirst=B&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbabel.hathitrust.org%2Fcgi%2Fpt%3Fid%3Ducm.5320214800%26view%3D1up%26seq%3D7&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATuberculosis"></span>  P. 51:  "The <i>Original</i> and <i>Essential Cause</i> ... may possibly be some certain Species of <i>Animalcula</i> or wonderfully minute living Creatures, ... "  P. 79:  "It may be therefore very likely, that by an habitual lying in the same Bed with a Consumptive Patient, constantly Eating and Drinking with him, or by very frequently conversing so nearly, as to draw in part of the Breath he emits from his Lungs, a Consumption may be caught by a sound Person; ... "</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-168"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-168">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source" id="CITEREFLaennec1819">Laennec RT (1819). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=LcZEAAAAcAAJ&amp;pg=PA20" rel="nofollow"><i>De l'auscultation médiate ...</i></a> (in French). Vol. 1. Paris, France: J.-A. Brosson et J.-S Chaudé. p. 20. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20210602212549/https://books.google.com/books?id=LcZEAAAAcAAJ&amp;pg=PA20" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> from the original on 2 June 2021<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">6 December</span> 2020</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=De+l%27auscultation+m%C3%A9diate+...&amp;rft.place=Paris%2C+France&amp;rft.pages=20&amp;rft.pub=J.-A.+Brosson+et+J.-S+Chaud%C3%A9&amp;rft.date=1819&amp;rft.aulast=Laennec&amp;rft.aufirst=RT&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DLcZEAAAAcAAJ%26pg%3DPA20&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATuberculosis"></span>  From p. 20: <i>"L'existence des tubercules dans le poumon est la cause et constitue le charactère anatomique propre de la phthisie pulmonaire (a).  (a) ... l'effet dont cette maladie tire son nom, c'est-à-dire, la consumption."</i> (The existence of tubercles in the lung is the cause and constitutes the unique anatomical characteristic of pulmonary tuberculosis (a).  (a) ... the effect from which this malady [pulmonary tuberculosis] takes its name, that is, consumption.)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-169"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-169">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1 cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source" id="CITEREFSchönlein1832">Schönlein JL (1832). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=zAtbAAAAcAAJ&amp;pg=PA103" rel="nofollow"><i>Allgemeine und specielle Pathologie und Therapie</i></a> [<i>General and Special Pathology and Therapy</i>] (in German). Etlinger. p. 103. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20210602233224/https://books.google.com/books?id=zAtbAAAAcAAJ&amp;pg=PA103" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> from the original on 2 June 2021<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">6 December</span> 2020</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Allgemeine+und+specielle+Pathologie+und+Therapie&amp;rft.place=W%C3%BCrzburg%2C+%28Germany%29&amp;rft.pages=103&amp;rft.pub=C.+Etlinger&amp;rft.date=1832&amp;rft.aulast=Sch%C3%B6nlein&amp;rft.aufirst=JL&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DzAtbAAAAcAAJ%26pg%3DPA103&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATuberculosis"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-170"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-170">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The word "tuberculosis" first appeared in Schönlein's clinical notes in 1829.  See: <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFJayKırbıyıkWoodsSteele2018">Jay SJ, Kırbıyık U, Woods JR, Steele GA, Hoyt GR, Schwengber RB, Gupta P (November 2018).
